The goal is to move away from rote learning and towards a more personalized, engaging experience. The AI technology will adapt to each student's learning needs and pace, providing tailored tasks and allowing teachers to monitor progress via digital dashboards. However, there is significant opposition from parents and academics who are concerned about the potential overexposure to digital devices and the risk of misinformation. More than 50,000 parents have petitioned against the plan, fearing negative effects on children's brain development and concentration. The drop in investment reflects the industry's struggle to maintain growth post-pandemic and the competition from AI-driven tools. Some edtech companies like Chegg and Coursera have seen substantial declines in stock value, while Duolingo has thrived by integrating AI features. Companies are racing to incorporate AI into their products, but skepticism remains regarding its impact on the education sector. Challenges such as high costs, bias, privacy concerns, and the rapid changes in technology have dampened investor enthusiasm.
